I absolutely love smoothies!!  They are one of my favorite breakfast items....except I made this one for my lunch today.  I love the oatmeal in it, but think that 1/2 a cup is a little too much.  I used quick cooking oats since that's what I normally have on hand and substituted a container of strawberry yogurt for the strawberries.  I have not been able to find a decent batch of strawberries yet this year. They are not sweet for some reason, so I'm a little hesitant to buy them.  Anyway, the oatmeal made this smoothie VERY filling and I too omitted the vanilla and sugar since I used vanilla flavored soy milk.  Great new find...thanks Astrophe.

text:
I LOVE this smoothie! I've made it literally hundreds of times since I first found it two years ago. It has just the right amount of sweetness, and it's thick and filling with the strawberries and oatmeal, so I often have it as a meal . Like others, I always process the oats first to a powder. I then add the milk, and I add just enough strawberries to meet the level of milk instead of counting them, since the size of the strawberries often varies. I find this gives it just the right consistency every time! Thanks for a great recipe!!

text:
This is for all smoothies that use raw oatmeal.  Soak oatmeal overnight or for 10 mins. in milk (1/2 c. to l c. milk)before adding to any smoothie to avoid any grainy texture.  Works great! I use this method for having cold oatmeal for breakfast during summer months and adding yogurt instead of milk overnight. Then add fresh fruit in morning for a delicious cold cereal.

text:
I eat oatmeal year round and found I like this smoothie better if I cook the oatmeal in the microwave first to absorb the liquid, then put it in the blender along with the frozen fruit, banana and additional milk.  Pre-cooking the oatmeal prevents the gritty texture and also the extra thickening that occurs when the uncooked ground oats start absorbing the liquid.  Much smoother texture this way and only adds about three extra minutes to the process.

city:

region:
None

text:
This was pretty good considering that my idea of eating oatmeal is when it's in cookies.  I used skim milk, sweetener, and added about 1/4 cup of pineapple chunks. I didn't use the vanilla.  My Vitamix blender whipped the drink into silky smoothness.  My husband loved it.  I have been making this for a couple of years.  I like having it for breakfast because it is very filling and keeps the munchies at bay.  In the beginning, I was having a hard time with the raw oats taste so I started lightly toasting the oats to see if that would ease the raw taste.  My husband says he can't tell the difference, but I can.  To toast the oats, I measure enough rolled oats to last for a week and place them on a large foil lined cookie sheet and lightly toast them at 300 degrees for a few minutes.  The oats need to be stirred a couple of times to keep them from burning.  They toast quickly. Once they are finished, I let them cool and grind them in my Vitamix and store the powder in a container.  I have also toasted the oats on top of the stove in a large skillet over medium heat.  I just stir them constantly until they start to smell like they are toasting (sort of nutty) and remove them from the heat, and the skillet.    I used the skillet method the first time I toasted them, and since it was an experiment, I only toasted a 1/2 cup of oats. Fortunately it worked it out for me!

It's very quick to make and it's healthy for you. Oh, when I'm out of strawberries, I use powdered chocolate (the one you use to make chocolate milk for kids). It tastes just as delicious as when you add strawberries, so if you run out of strawberries, you can substitute it with chocolate. I definitely recommend this for people who want to make a quick healthy, delicious AND FILLING breakfast smoothie. If you usually don't have time to sit and eat breakfast at the table like me, I highly recommend you to try this recipe at least once. It's very good :)

text:
This recipe has become our standard breakfast for the past 6 months -- thanks so much!!  My system is to layer the oatmeal, then banana, then plain soy milk in the blender and let that soak while we have our morning coffee (about half an hour).  Then I blend those 3 together at a high speed to break up the oatmeal.  Then I add a small handful of frozen raspberries and blend thoroughly; then about 8-10 frozen strawberries and blend again.  It makes enough for my husband to have a full glass and for me to have about 2/3 of a glass.  We love having all these healthy things to start our day and we don't feel the need to add any sweeteners or other  ingredients.  So yummy!

I first made it exactly as written for 2 servings, except that I did substitute non-fat milk for the soy milk, and I used a pack of Sweet and Low instead of white sugar. It was great, but a little thin.  So I threw in 6 ice cubes, and it was perfect!  Thanks to all the previous reviewers for making this sound so good that curiosity made me try it.  I'm going to compute the "points" and share it with my Weight Watcher friends. (and I'm going to experiment with some mango and peaches, etc.)

text:
I recently bought a personal blender and was looking for a good smoothie recipe with which to break it in. I settled on this one and BOY was it a good choice. I've been making them all week. The only changes I make are that I use regular 2% milk and about 8 frozen strawberries because 14 is just too many for my small blender. I also blend the oats first, then add the milk and strawberries and top with the bananas, sugar, and vanilla. It turns out perfectly. As others have said, it's filling, but it didn't overdo it for me. It's a good snack or healthy dessert after a smaller meal. The oats are a nice touch that I never would have thought to use. I know I'll be making this recipe long into the future.

After many times making this I came up with my own delicious modified version:  

1/4 cup oat (75 cals)
1 cup unsweetened almond vanilla milk (35 cals)
10 frozen strawberries (40 cals)
1 banana (100 cals)
1 tsp vanilla extract
2 packets Truvia.  

SO yummy filling, and just 250 calories for the entire thing!

To be fair, I rated this recipe in Jan 2011 and now again tried it in Jan 2014. The first time I tried it I had a different blender and did not care for it due to the oatmeal being so prominent and I didn't like drinking gummy hard bits of uncooked oatmeal, according to my old review. I'm definitely going to use soy milk in the future, though, since it has more vitamins, etc, than regular milk.

text:
I make smoothies often in my NutriBullet, not to loose weight but to eat healthier.. I add a smoothie in between meals to make sure I get in my daily required fruits and vegetables. I've never had oatmeal in a smoothie and thought this would be a great change. This was really good!!!  I made a few changes.  I added kale, vanilla soy milk, and apple juice. I omitted the sugar because the banana and apple juice were enough sweeteners. I tore up a whole leafy kale stem, added sliced bananas, frozen strawberries, 1/3 cup oats, a little vanilla flavor, and filled the cup with 1/2 vanilla soy milk and 1/2 apple juice up to the"Max" line ( I used the large cup serving).  I don't like thick smoothies so I wanted to make sure I had enough liquid to absorb the oats and still have the right consistency. I did taste a little grittiness as some reviewers noted but not enough to bother. The NutriBullet does a great job mixing/chopping/blending fruits, nuts, and vegetables anyway.  Now that I like it next time I'll add flax seeds as one reviewer wrote!

I love the idea of oatmeal in a smoothie! I always grind the oatmeal in the blender first for a smoother consistency. I also like to add flax seed for some additional nutrients. I like my smoothies to have a thicker consistency so I always add plain yogurt and reduce the milk or just omit it all together and maybe add some fresh juice. I've tried all kinds of fruit in these and they are all delicious. I like to make a big batch and store it in a pitcher in the fridge so that in the mornings I can just pour a tall glass of smoothie for a great on-the-go breakfast!

Yummy yummy!! Can I give it ten stars? Because that's what I feel it deserves. I followed the advice of many other reviews and blended my oats a little first and I think that made a big difference. I did change a lot of the recipe... in fact pretty much all of it... to fit what I had on hand and my tastes, but the oatmeal idea is genius. I can't wait to make this again.

Hello all! I was up earlier than usual this AM (considering I am unemployed & do not need to get up early to go to work...), and, after a couple of hrs., the hunger pains set in! I wanted a quick-fix. Michelle's smoothie fit the bill perfectly! And, who would have thought of using oatmeal as a thickener... genius! While I agree w/ some (that this was a tad lacking in flavor - I guess I like my smoothies extra sweet!), it was yummy nonetheless. Since I had planned on making this last wk. (but I never got around to it...), I ended up freezing my fruit for later use. Today, all I had to do was remove what I needed, add the rest of the ing. and voila - a thick, creamy & filling smoothie! My only change was to use vanilla flavored soy milk (whole, skim or ff would also be fine) and omit the extract. I think I will add OJ next time or maybe sub. raspberries for strawberries (I think it's the tang that is missing). A mixed berry combo (i.e. blueberries, strawberries, blackberries, raspberries) would be an excellent sub. too If your store only sells sweetened mixed berries, omit the sugar called for.  Oh, and I think Jeanbean1001's idea to use an instant oatmeal pk. (cinnamon - yum, yum!) is an EXCELLENT idea (I will try this next time!). I will DEFINITELY be serving this at my next brunch AND as a quick  "on the go" pick-me-up on those all to often busy mornings (w/ my noted changes, of course). Thx. for sharing, Michelle :)

text:
I made this for breakfast today because I ran out of eggs and needed something to hold up my family up until I went and got groceries later.
I doubled the recipe and ground up steel cut oats first until it was a fine powder. Then I ground up raw almonds until it was also a fine powder. Then I added the low fat milk and the other ingredients, except the vanilla because I was out of that too.   My bananas and strawberries were frozen so I was getting a mixture that was looking like ice cream so I let it sit for a bit. I blended it more until is was more like a smoothie and tried it. I ended up adding more sugar otherwise the kids would not drink it but I thoroughly enjoyed it. I will def make again and add vanilla next time. I used all organic ingredients so I'm sure it's very nutritious and healthy. I will continue to use almonds as well as oats since I think it makes it even more filling and satisfying. Thanks for the recipe!

It was really thick (I think I used too many strawberries), so I added a half a can of peach nectar juice to thin it out and to give it a little bit more sweetness and let me tell you it was DELICIOUS!  It was really filling and held me all the way to lunch.  This will become a regular.

text:
This recipe is awesome! As a few others have done, I ground the oats to a fine powder first. But then I blended my silk vanilla soy milk with it before adding the fruit. It blended much better this way. I also omitted the vanilla extract because I used the vanilla soy milk. This was very fulfilling it kept me energized right through to lunch time. One thing I will say is if you aren't really an oatmeal person I suggest using a little less than what the recipe calls for because you can really taste the oats, not more than the strawberries and bananas though. Added bonus: this is a great recipe for those who are lactose intolerant.

This was yummy! I did tweak it a bit though. Since I drink almond milk b/c it is creamier than soy, I added a cup of that. I think next time Ill try another persons idea and use vanilla flavored almond milk next time like i used to add to my summertime smoothies. Next time i hope to have just strawberries on hand. Reason I gave it 4 stars not 5 was b/c it does call for added sugar which with the soy milk and fruit I didnt feel adding more sugar would be a great breakfast idea to avoid that mid day crash. All in all, great ratio's and a very tasty and quick breakfast. Kept me full for a while.

text:
I LOVE using raw oatmeal in my smoothies.  I grind up my oatmeal first in the blender really fine.  Then I add crushed ice and vanilla soy milk.  Grind that all together and then add a frozen banana, some plain fat free greek yogurt, some decaffeinated instant coffee granules for flavor, a little bit of honey and blend it up real good.  OH MY GOSH...best smoothie I've ever had.  I have this every morning for breakfast.  So healthy and delish!  Try it, you'll love it.

text:
Sorry but I just don't like the oats in there.  It wasn't the texture.  I tend to give a little whir to anything frozen first, then add other stuff and add only enough milk at a time to be able to blend, so that everything gets blended as smoothly as possible.  (Don't like ending up with 'pulp'.)  So the oats just blended fine with everything else.  Granted it was more filling than some smoothies but I didn't like the taste of the oats in there.  It wasn't bad - just not great.  I've actually made it several times trying to play with it (but still mostly sticking to the recipe), like I've used both fresh & frozen, and 1% milk and nonfat dry milk (don't have soy).  I also reduced the oats by half and it still tasted too much like oats.  (And I'm sorry, but adding things like blueberries would so incredibly change the taste that it wouldn't be this recipe anymore.)

I drink a lot of smoothies and I never thought to add oatmeal or vanilla, so for giving me a healthy new way to make smoothies I give this five stars!! I like honey instead of sugar, and like to add some plain yogurt to my smoothies to get the added benefit of yogurt. Thank you for the new recipe - this can so easily be adapted (different fruits, milk instead of soy milk, add yogurt, etc.) I will make many variations of this!
P.S. A very healthy addition to any smoothie is 1-2 teaspoons of ground flax seed - found at Trader Joe's or health food stores.

text:
I love strawberries, I love oatmeal, I love banana's and often make hot oatmeal with vanilla, almond milk, strawberries and banana. However, mixed as a cold smoothie I'm not digging too much. I actually processed the oatmeal into a fine powder and then used and somehow it still came out grainy. The oatmeal flavor is overpowering the banana and strawberries which says a lot since this calls for so many strawberries. If I were to make again I think I am going to knock the amount of oatmeal down considerably and possibly add a little more strawberries and a second banana. As it's written I don't really care for it and wouldn't make it again. With my moderations it might be bearable. On a side note if you use normal almond milk you shouldn't need sugar as it might come out being too sugary, if using unsweetened almond milk definitely add the sugar because it might come out bitter depending on how sweet your fruit is.

text:
I LOVE strawberry-banana smoothies, but I could never get the right proportions when making it at home.  These are the right proportions.  Like everyone else, I blend the oats first to get them to a powdery consistency.  I find it plenty sweet on its own, and don't use the sugar or vanilla extract (I did at first).  The recipe is for 2 servings, but I'm the only one drinking it so I cut it in half.  I use about 2/3 of a banana for each serving, and I freeze them in individual portions so I don't always have to keep bananas on hand.  BUT they MUST be defrosted when you're blending, otherwise it will take forever.  Usually I defrost them overnight, or for a few hours in the morning.  They don't look too appealing when defrosted but I freeze them when they're ripe and they're going in a smoothie anyway, so who cares.  I buy a big bag of frozen strawberries from the store and find it to be way less work than freezing my own.  Great recipe!

text:
i have made this recipe exactly as listed and it was fantastic!  However, I also made it without the vanilla and the sugar and it is still pretty great, and healthier! Plus I usually make this at work and don't have vanilla on me. 
A few notes: it is important to use the frozen strawberries or even frozen bananas.  This makes it colder, the proper temperature.
If you do not like the consistency of oatmeal, grind it up before hand.  

You can substitute pretty much any fruits in here, but I'd leave the banana in.  Keep in mind, the other fruits won't taste as strong as the strawberry.

text:
This is definitely two servings like the original recipe says, I don't know how people can drink the whole thing! I put the rest in a large thermos that I am taking to work, so I can smoothie throughout the morning.  I almost folllowed the recipe... I did 1/2 cup 2% milk and 1/3 non fat yogurt. I also only did 9 strawberries (mine were huge). I ended up finding it too thick, so I added 1/3 cup water just to thin it out at the end (I didn't want to add any more fat from the milk, and it tastes just the same at this stage of the recipe).   I really enjoyed this smoothie. You can taste the oats, and you can tell in the texture that they are there, but I think it's quite delicious.

I got up with my husband this morning just to make him this smoothie and use up some of our fresh strawberries and bananas (didn't find that it was too runny with nothing frozen. The oats thicken it up I think). I used light soy milk and made sure to powder the oats first before adding the liquids (texture preference). I wasn't terribly precise in measuring the strawberries. I just put in a couple big scoops, maybe a cup and a half. No sugar was needed in addition to the main ingredients but I added the vanilla because I love it! I think I will start adding oatmeal to all my smoothies for health reasons. I could hardly taste it and it helped fill me up so I didn't overindulge. This made about 6dl of smoothie in my estimation. Thanks!

text:
This is a really good recipe. I use slightly less than 1/2 cup of oatmeal finely ground and add a few packets of sweetner. I also used 2/3rd cup of unsweetened almond milk because I wanted the smoothie really thick. If you allow the smoothie to sit for a few minutes before serving it gives the oatflour time to absorb some of the liquid which eliminates the "chalky" taste that some complain of. This is definately going in our rotation.
